The partition of Rwanda following the RPF offensive in February 1993. For the first time, the Rwandan government acknowledged that it had lost part of the country.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The RPF went back on the offensive on 8 February, fighting south from the positions it already held on Rwanda's northern border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174_132-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174-132">[132]</a></sup> In contrast to the October 1990 and the 1991–92 campaigns, the RPF advance in 1993 was met with only weak resistance from the Rwandan government's FAR forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174_132-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174-132">[132]</a></sup> The likely reason for this is a significant deterioration in morale and military experience in those forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174_132-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174-132">[132]</a></sup> The impact of the long running war on the economy, and a heavy devaluation of the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_franc" title="Rwandan franc">Rwandan franc</a> compared to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999159_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999159-134">[134]</a></sup> had left the government unable to pay its soldiers in a timely manner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174_132-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174-132">[132]</a></sup> The armed forces had also expanded rapidly, at one point growing from less than 10,000 troops to almost 30,000 in one year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMelvern200420_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMelvern200420-135">[135]</a></sup> The new recruits were often poorly disciplined and not battle ready,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMelvern200420_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMelvern200420-135">[135]</a></sup> with a tendency to get drunk and carry out abuse and rapes of civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174_132-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999174-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>The RPF advance was unchecked, moving steadily south and gaining territory without opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175-136">[136]</a></sup> They took Ruhengeri on the first day of fighting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175-136">[136]</a></sup> and later the city of <a href="/wiki/Byumba" title="Byumba">Byumba</a>. As with the previous RPF advances, the Hutu civilians in the area fled en masse from the areas the RPF were claiming, back into the government controlled territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175_136-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175-136">[136]</a></sup> These exoduses were likely driven primarily by the fear of the RPF established by years of propaganda,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175_136-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175-136">[136]</a></sup> although the RPF soldiers were guilty in some areas of small scale killing of Hutu civilians; this was partly in retribution for the massacre of Tutsi perpetrated in these areas in late January, but there was some indiscriminate killing also.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175_136-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175-136">[136]</a></sup> These killings increased the fear felt by the Hutu population, but also served to further alienate the RPF from its potential allies in the democratic Rwandan opposition parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999176_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999176-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>The RPF advance caused panic in France, a long term supporter of the Habyarimana regime, which immediately sent several hundred French troops to the country along with arms and ammunition to bolster the FAR forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999176_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999176-137">[137]</a></sup> The arrival of these French troops in Kigali seriously changed the military situation on the ground. The RPF now found themselves under attack, with French shells bombarding them as they advanced southwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008105_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008105-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 20 February the RPF had advanced to within 30 km (19 mi) of the capital, <a href="/wiki/Kigali" title="Kigali">Kigali</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999177_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999177-139">[139]</a></sup> and many observers believed an assault on the city to be imminent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175_136-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999175-136">[136]</a></sup> The assault did not happen, however, and the RPF instead declared a ceasefire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999177_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999177-139">[139]</a></sup> Whether or not the RPF actually intended to advance on the capital is unknown. Kagame later stated that his aim at this point, despite a desire in his senior officers to go for outright victory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008105_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008105-138">[138]</a></sup> was to inflict as much damage as possible on FAR forces, capture their weapons, and gain ground slowly, but not to attack the capital itself, and possibly end the war with outright RPF victory, since that would end international goodwill towards the RPF and lead to charges that the intention of the war was simply to replace a Hutu state with a Tutsi one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008104_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008104-133">[133]</a></sup> However, the increased presence of French troops on the ground, and the fierce loyalty of the Hutu population to the government, meant that despite the ease with which the RPF conquered the north, fighting for the capital could prove a much more difficult and potentially dangerous operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999178_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999178-140">[140]</a></sup> By the end of the February war, over one million civilians, mostly Hutu, had left their homes, in the country's largest exodus to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008105_138-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008105-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arusha_Accords_and_rise_of_Hutu_Power.2C_1993.E2.80.9394">Arusha Accords and rise of Hutu Power, 1993–94</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rwandan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Arusha Accords and rise of Hutu Power, 1993–94">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AICC_Arusha.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2478" data-file-width="3648" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/AICC_Arusha.jpg/220px-AICC_Arusha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/AICC_Arusha.jpg/330px-AICC_Arusha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/AICC_Arusha.jpg/440px-AICC_Arusha.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AICC_Arusha.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Arusha_International_Conference_Centre" title="Arusha International Conference Centre">Arusha International Conference Centre</a>, venue for peace talks to end the war.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arusha_accords" title="Arusha accords">Arusha accords</a></div>
<p>The RPF ceasefire was followed by two days of negotiations in the Ugandan capital <a href="/wiki/Kampala" title="Kampala">Kampala</a>, attended by RPF leader Paul Kagame, and involving President Museveni and representatives of European nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106-141">[141]</a></sup> The Europeans insisted that the RPF forces withdraw to the zone they had held before the February offensive, while Kagame insisted that he would only agree to this if the Rwandan army were forbidden from re-entering the newly conquered territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106-141">[141]</a></sup> Following a threat by Kagame to resume fighting and potentially take even more territory, the two sides reached a compromise deal whereby the RPF would withdraw to its pre-February territory, but a de-militarised zone would be set up between the RPF area and the rest of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106_141-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106-141">[141]</a></sup> The deal was significant, because it marked a formal concession by Habyarimana's regime of the northern zone to the rebels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106_141-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106-141">[141]</a></sup> However, there were many within the RPF senior command who felt that Kagame had ceded too much, because the deal meant not only withdrawal to the pre-February boundaries, but also a promise not to encroach on the de-militarised zone, and therefore an end to RPF ambitions of capturing more territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106_141-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008106-141">[141]</a></sup> Kagame used the authority he'd accumulated through his successful leadership of the RPF to override these concerns, and the parties returned once more to the negotiating table in Arusha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008107_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008107-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the agreement and ongoing negotiations, President Habyarimana, supported by the French government,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999178_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999178-140">[140]</a></sup> spent the subsequent months forging a "common front" against the RPF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999179_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999179-143">[143]</a></sup> This included members of his own party and the CDR, and also factions from each of the other opposition parties in the power sharing coalition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999179_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999179-143">[143]</a></sup> Simultaneously, however, other members of the same parties issued a statement in conjunction with the RPF, in which they condemned French involvement in the country and called for the Arusha process to be respected in full.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999179_143-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999179-143">[143]</a></sup> The hardline factions within the parties became known as <a href="/wiki/Hutu_Power" title="Hutu Power">Hutu Power</a>, a movement which transcended party politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999188_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999188-144">[144]</a></sup> Apart from the CDR, there was no party that was exclusively part of the Power movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999181_182_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999181_182-145">[145]</a></sup> Instead, almost every party was split into "moderate" and "Power" wings, with members of both camps claiming to represent the legitimate leadership of that party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999181_182_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999181_182-145">[145]</a></sup> Even the ruling party contained a Power wing, consisting of those who opposed Habyarimana's intention to sign a peace deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999182_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999182-146">[146]</a></sup> Several radical youth militia groups emerged, attached to the Power wings of the parties; these included the <i><a href="/wiki/Interahamwe" title="Interahamwe">Interahamwe</a></i>, which was attached to the ruling party,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003129_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003129-147">[147]</a></sup> and the CDR's <i><a href="/wiki/Impuzamugambi" title="Impuzamugambi">Impuzamugambi</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999165_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999165-148">[148]</a></sup> The youth militia began actively carrying out massacres across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMelvern200425_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMelvern200425-149">[149]</a></sup> The army trained the militias, sometimes in conjunction with the French, who were unaware of their true purpose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999165_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999165-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>By June, President Habyarimana had come to view Hutu Power as a bigger threat to his leadership than the mainstream opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999186_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999186-150">[150]</a></sup> This led him to engage fully once more with the Arusha peace process, giving it the impetus it needed to draw to a completion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999186_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999186-150">[150]</a></sup> According to historian <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A9rard_Prunier" title="Gérard Prunier">Gérard Prunier</a>, this support was more symbolic than truly meant, with Habyarimana believing himself capable of staying in power through a combination of limited concessions through peace, along with strategic small scale violence where necessary, and that this would be much harder to achieve if the peace process broke down and Hutu Power rose to supremacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999186_150-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999186-150">[150]</a></sup> The RPF enjoyed much greater leverage following their successful February campaign, and their power-sharing demands, including up to 40% of the troops in the proposed unified national armed forces, and 50% of the officer corps, were eventually agreed to in full by the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999193_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999193-151">[151]</a></sup> With all details the agreed, the <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Accords" title="Arusha Accords">Arusha Accords</a> were finally signed on 4 August 1993 at a formal ceremony attended by President Habyarimana as well as heads of state from neighbouring countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999191_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999191-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>An uneasy peace was once again entered into, which would last until 7 April of the following year. The agreement called for a United Nations <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> force, and Canadian general <a href="/wiki/Rom%C3%A9o_Dallaire" title="Roméo Dallaire">Roméo Dallaire</a> was selected to head this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire200342_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire200342-153">[153]</a></sup> Dallaire made a preliminary visit in late August,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire200357_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire200357-154">[154]</a></sup> and the force, titled the United Nations Assistance Mission for Rwanda (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Assistance_Mission_for_Rwanda" title="United Nations Assistance Mission for Rwanda">UNAMIR</a>), was in place in Rwanda by October 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire200398_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire200398-155">[155]</a></sup> Another stipulation of the agreement was that the RPF would station a number of diplomats in Kigali at the <i>Conseil national de développement</i> (CND), now known as the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Rwanda)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Rwanda)">Chamber of Deputies</a>, Rwanda's parliament building.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003130_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003130-156">[156]</a></sup> These men were protected by between 600-1000 RPF soldiers, who arrived in Kigali in <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Operation_Clean_Corridor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Operation Clean Corridor (page does not exist)">Operation Clean Corridor</a> in December 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003130_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003130-156">[156]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Hutu Power wings of the various parties were actively beginning plans for what would be come the 1994 <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200-157">[157]</a></sup> The President of Burundi, <a href="/wiki/Melchior_Ndadaye" title="Melchior Ndadaye">Melchior Ndadaye</a>, who had been elected in June as the country's first ever Hutu president, was assassinated by extremist Tutsi army officers in October 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999199_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999199-158">[158]</a></sup> The assassination caused shockwaves, reinforcing the notion among Hutus that the Tutsi were their enemy and could not be trusted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200-157">[157]</a></sup> The CDR and the Power wings of the other parties realised they could use this situation to their advantage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200_157-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200-157">[157]</a></sup> The idea of a "final solution," which had first been suggested in 1992 but had remained a fringe viewpoint, was now top of their agenda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200_157-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999200-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_operations_during_the_1994_genocide">Military operations during the 1994 genocide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rwandan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military operations during the 1994 genocide">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1130" height="230" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg/300px-RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg/450px-RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg/600px-RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RPF_advance_Rwandan_Genocide_1994.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map showing the advance of the RPF during the Rwandan Genocide of 1994</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The cease-fire ended abruptly on 6 April 1994, when Rwandan President Habyarimana's plane <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Juv%C3%A9nal_Habyarimana_and_Cyprien_Ntaryamira" title="Assassination of Juvénal Habyarimana and Cyprien Ntaryamira">was shot down</a> near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kigali_Airport" title="Kigali Airport">Kigali Airport</a>, killing both Habyarimana and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Burundi" title="List of Presidents of Burundi">President of Burundi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprien_Ntaryamira" title="Cyprien Ntaryamira">Cyprien Ntaryamira</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Assembly_of_France1998_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Assembly_of_France1998-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28I.292010_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28I.292010-160">[160]</a></sup> The attackers remain unknown. Gérard Prunier, in his book written shortly after the incident, concluded that it was most likely a coup d'État carried out by extreme Hutu members of Habyarimana's government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999222.E2.80.93223_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999222.E2.80.93223-161">[161]</a></sup> This theory was disputed in 2006 by French judge <a href="/wiki/Jean-Louis_Brugui%C3%A8re" title="Jean-Louis Bruguière">Jean-Louis Bruguière</a>, and in 2008 by Spanish judge <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Andreu" title="Fernando Andreu">Fernando Andreu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2008_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2008-162">[162]</a></sup> Both alleged that Kagame and the RPF were responsible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrugui.C3.A8re20061_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrugui.C3.A8re20061-163">[163]</a></sup> At the end of 2010 the French government ordered a more thorough judicial inquiry, which employed ballistics experts. This report reaffirmed the initial theory that Hutu extremists assassinated Habyarimana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28XX.292012_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28XX.292012-164">[164]</a></sup> The shooting down of the plane served as the catalyst for the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_genocide" title="Rwandan genocide">Rwandan genocide</a>, which began within a few hours. An interim government took over, headed by <i>de facto</i> leader Colonel Théoneste Bagosora, which began ordering the systematic killing of huge numbers of Tutsi, as well as some politically moderate Hutu, through well-planned attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003386_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003386-165">[165]</a></sup> Over the course of approximately 100 days, between 500,000 and 1,000,000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenley2007_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenley2007-166">[166]</a></sup> were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003386_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003386-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 April, as the genocide started, RPF commander Paul Kagame warned the crisis committee and UNAMIR that he would resume the civil war if the killing did not stop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003247_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003247-167">[167]</a></sup> The next day, Rwandan government FAR forces attacked the national parliament building from several directions, but RPF troops stationed there successfully fought back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003264.E2.80.93265_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003264.E2.80.93265-168">[168]</a></sup> The RPF then began an attack from the north on three fronts, seeking to link up quickly with the isolated troops in Kigali.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003269_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003269-169">[169]</a></sup> Kagame refused to talk to the interim government, believing that it was just a cover for Bagosora's rule and not committed to ending the genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999268_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999268-170">[170]</a></sup> Over the next few days, the RPF advanced steadily south, capturing <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gabiro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gabiro (page does not exist)">Gabiro</a> and large areas of the countryside to the north and east of Kigali.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003288_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003288-171">[171]</a></sup> They avoided attacking Kigali or Byumba, but conducted manoeuvres designed to encircle the cities and cut off supply routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003299_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003299-172">[172]</a></sup> The RPF also allowed Tutsi refugees from Uganda to settle behind the front line in the RPF controlled areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003299_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003299-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout April, there were numerous attempts by UNAMIR to establish a ceasefire, but Kagame insisted each time that the RPF would not stop fighting unless the killings stopped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003300_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003300-173">[173]</a></sup> In late April, the RPF secured the whole of the Tanzanian border area and began to move west from Kibungo, to the south of Kigali.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003326.E2.80.93327_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003326.E2.80.93327-174">[174]</a></sup> They encountered little resistance, except around Kigali and Ruhengeri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999268_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999268-170">[170]</a></sup> By 16 May, they had cut the road between Kigali and <a href="/wiki/Gitarama" title="Gitarama">Gitarama</a>, the temporary home of the interim government, and by 13 June, had taken Gitarama itself, following an unsuccessful attempt by the FAR forces to reopen the road; the interim government was forced to relocate to Gisenyi in the far north west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003410_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003410-175">[175]</a></sup> As well as fighting the war, Kagame was recruiting heavily to expand the army. The new recruits included Tutsi survivors of the genocide and refugees from Burundi, but were less well trained and disciplined than the earlier recruits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999270_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999270-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>Having completed the encirclement of Kigali, the RPF spent the latter half of June fighting for the city itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421-177">[177]</a></sup> The FAR forces had superior manpower and weapons, but the RPF steadily gained territory as well as conducting raids to rescue civilians from behind enemy lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421-177">[177]</a></sup> According to Dallaire, this success was due to Kagame's being a "master of psychological warfare";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421_177-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421-177">[177]</a></sup> he exploited the fact that the FAR were concentrating on the genocide rather than the fight for Kigali, and capitalised on the government's loss of morale as it lost territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421_177-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003421-177">[177]</a></sup> The RPF finally defeated the FAR in Kigali on 4 July,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003459_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003459-178">[178]</a></sup> and on 18 July took Gisenyi and the rest of the northwest, forcing the interim government into Zaire and ending the genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999298.E2.80.93299_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999298.E2.80.93299-179">[179]</a></sup> At the end of July 1994, Kagame's forces held the whole of Rwanda except for the zone in the south west which had been occupied by a French-led United Nations force as part of <a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ration_Turquoise" title="Opération Turquoise">Opération Turquoise</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003474.E2.80.93475_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDallaire2003474.E2.80.93475-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Day" title="Liberation Day">Liberation Day</a> for Rwanda would come to be marked as July 4 and is commemorated as <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Rwanda" title="Public holidays in Rwanda">a public holiday</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rwandan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_situation">Domestic situation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rwandan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Domestic situation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rwanda-demography.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="725" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Rwanda-demography.png/220px-Rwanda-demography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Rwanda-demography.png/330px-Rwanda-demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Rwanda-demography.png/440px-Rwanda-demography.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rwanda-demography.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Graph showing the population of Rwanda from 1961 to 2003. (Data from U.N. <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The victorious RPF assumed control of the country following the genocide, and as of 2017 remain the dominant political force in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The infrastructure and economy of the country had suffered greatly during the genocide. Many buildings were uninhabitable, and the former regime had carried with them all currency and moveable assets when they fled the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008181_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008181-183">[183]</a></sup> Human resources were also severely depleted, with over <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7001400000000000000♠</span>40% of the population having been killed or fled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008181_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008181-183">[183]</a></sup> Many of the remainder were traumatised: most had lost relatives, witnessed killings or participated in the genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnited_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_States_Holocaust_Memorial_Museum-184">[184]</a></sup> The long-term effects of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_rape" title="War rape">war rape</a> in Rwanda for the victims include social isolation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_diseases" title="Sexually transmitted diseases">sexually transmitted diseases</a>, unwanted pregnancies and babies, with some women resorted to self-induced abortions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-de_Brouwer_2005_14_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-de_Brouwer_2005_14-185">[185]</a></sup> The army, led by Paul Kagame, maintained law and order while the government began the work of rebuilding the country's structures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBonner1994_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonner1994-186">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008187_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008187-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">Non-governmental organisations</a> began to move back into the country, but the international community did not provide significant assistance to the new regime, and most <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">international aid</a> was routed to the refugee camps which had formed in Zaire following the exodus of Hutu from Rwanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999327.E2.80.93328_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999327.E2.80.93328-188">[188]</a></sup> Kagame strove to portray the government as inclusive and not Tutsi dominated. He directed removal of ethnicity from citizens' national identity cards, and the government began a policy of downplaying the distinctions among Hutu, Tutsi, and Twa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBonner1994_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonner1994-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the genocide and in the months following the RPF victory, RPF soldiers killed many people they accused of participating in or supporting the genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008189_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008189-189">[189]</a></sup> Many of these soldiers were recent Tutsi recruits from within Rwanda, who had lost family or friends and sought revenge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008189_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008189-189">[189]</a></sup> The scale, scope, and source of ultimate responsibility of these killings is disputed. <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, as well as scholars such as Prunier, allege that the death toll might be as high as 100,000,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999360_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999360-190">[190]</a></sup> and that Kagame and the RPF elite either tolerated or organised the killings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_Watch_.28I.291999_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuman_Rights_Watch_.28I.291999-191">[191]</a></sup> In an interview with journalist <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Kinzer" title="Stephen Kinzer">Stephen Kinzer</a>, Kagame acknowledged that killings had occurred but stated that they were carried out by rogue soldiers and had been impossible to control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008191_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008191-192">[192]</a></sup> The RPF killings gained international attention with the 1995 <a href="/wiki/Kibeho_massacre" title="Kibeho massacre">Kibeho massacre</a>, in which soldiers opened fire on a camp for internally displaced persons in <a href="/wiki/Butare_Province" title="Butare Province">Butare Province</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELorch1995_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELorch1995-193">[193]</a></sup> Australian soldiers serving as part of UNAMIR estimated at least 4,000 people were killed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustralian_War_Memorial_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustralian_War_Memorial-194">[194]</a></sup> while the Rwandan government claimed that the death toll was 338.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier200942_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier200942-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>Paul Kagame took over the presidency from <a href="/wiki/Pasteur_Bizimungu" title="Pasteur Bizimungu">Pasteur Bizimungu</a> in 2000,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28V.292000_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28V.292000-196">[196]</a></sup> and began a large-scale national development drive, launching <a href="/wiki/Vision_2020_(Rwanda)" title="Vision 2020 (Rwanda)">a programme</a> to develop Rwanda as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_income_country" title="Middle income country">middle income country</a> by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008226.E2.80.93227_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008226.E2.80.93227-197">[197]</a></sup> The country began developing strongly on key indicators, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_development_index" title="Human development index">human development index</a>, health care and education; annual growth between 2004 and 2010 averaged <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">7000800000000000000♠</span>8% per year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurdock2010_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurdock2010-198">[198]</a></sup> the poverty rate reduced from 57% to 45% between 2006 and 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2012_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Institute_of_Statistics_of_Rwanda2012-199">[199]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> rose from 46.6 years in 2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUNDP_.28V.2920132_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUNDP_.28V.2920132-200">[200]</a></sup> to 59.7 years in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECIA_.28I.29_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECIA_.28I.29-201">[201]</a></sup> A period of reconciliation and justice began, with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_Rwanda" title="International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda">International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda</a> (ICTR) and the reintroduction of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gacaca" title="Gacaca">Gacaca</a></i>, a traditional village court system.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugee_crisis.2C_insurgency.2C_and_Congo_wars">Refugee crisis, insurgency, and Congo wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rwandan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Refugee crisis, insurgency, and Congo wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_refugee_crisis" title="Great Lakes refugee crisis">Great Lakes refugee crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg"><img alt="View of refugee camp on foggy day, showing tents of various colours and the refugees" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg/220px-Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg/330px-Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg/440px-Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rwandan_refugee_camp_in_east_Zaire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Refugee_camp" title="Refugee camp">Refugee camp</a> in <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>, 1994</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the RPF victory, approximately two million Hutu fled to refugee camps in neighbouring countries, particularly Zaire, fearing RPF reprisals for the Rwandan Genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999312_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999312-202">[202]</a></sup> The camps were crowded and squalid, and thousands of refugees died in disease epidemics, including <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The camps were set up by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a> (UNHCR), but were effectively controlled by the army and government of the former Hutu regime, including many leaders of the genocide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999313.E2.80.93314_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999313.E2.80.93314-204">[204]</a></sup> who began rearming in a bid to return to power in Rwanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999381.E2.80.93382_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999381.E2.80.93382-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997-206">[206]</a></sup></p>
<p>By late 1996, Hutu militants from the camps were launching regular cross-border incursions, and the RPF-led Rwandan government launched a counteroffensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999382_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999382-207">[207]</a></sup> Rwanda provided troops and military training<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997-206">[206]</a></sup> to the <a href="/wiki/Banyamulenge" title="Banyamulenge">Banyamulenge</a>, a Tutsi group in the Zairian <a href="/wiki/South_Kivu" title="South Kivu">South Kivu</a> province,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999384.E2.80.93385_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999384.E2.80.93385-208">[208]</a></sup> helping them to defeat Zairian security forces. Rwandan forces, the Banyamulenge, and other Zairian Tutsi, then attacked the refugee camps, targeting the Hutu militia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999384.E2.80.93385_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier1999384.E2.80.93385-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997_206-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997-206">[206]</a></sup> These attacks caused hundreds of thousands of refugees to flee;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009118_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009118-209">[209]</a></sup> many returned to Rwanda despite the presence of the RPF, while others ventured further west into Zaire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009122.E2.80.93123_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009122.E2.80.93123-210">[210]</a></sup> The defeated forces of the former regime continued a cross-border insurgency campaign,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008209_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008209-211">[211]</a></sup> supported initially by the predominantly Hutu population of Rwanda's north western provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008216_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008216-212">[212]</a></sup> By 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrittain1999_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrittain1999-213">[213]</a></sup> a programme of propaganda and Hutu integration into the <a href="/wiki/Rwandan_Defence_Forces" title="Rwandan Defence Forces">national army</a>, succeeded in bringing the Hutu to the government side and the insurgency was defeated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008215.E2.80.93218_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinzer2008215.E2.80.93218-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to dismantling the refugee camps, Kagame began planning a war to remove long-time dictator President <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a> from power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997_206-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomfret1997-206">[206]</a></sup> Mobutu had supported the <i>genocidaires</i> based in the camps, and was also accused of allowing attacks on Tutsi people within Zaire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBymanChalkHoffmanRosenau200118_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBymanChalkHoffmanRosenau200118-215">[215]</a></sup> Together with Uganda, the Rwandan government supported an alliance of four rebel groups headed by <a href="/wiki/Laurent-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Kabila" title="Laurent-Désiré Kabila">Laurent-Désiré Kabila</a>, which began waging the <a href="/wiki/First_Congo_War" title="First Congo War">First Congo War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009113.E2.80.93116_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009113.E2.80.93116-216">[216]</a></sup> The rebels quickly took control of North and South Kivu provinces and then advanced west, gaining territory from the poorly organised and demotivated Zairian army with little fighting,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009128.E2.80.93133_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009128.E2.80.93133-217">[217]</a></sup> and controlling the whole country by May 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009136_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009136-218">[218]</a></sup> Mobutu fled into exile, and the country was renamed <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (DRC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28II.29_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28II.29-219">[219]</a></sup> Rwanda fell out with the new Congolese regime in 1998, and Kagame supported a fresh rebellion, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Congo_War" title="Second Congo War">Second Congo War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009182.E2.80.93183_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrunier2009182.E2.80.93183-220">[220]</a></sup> This war lasted until 2003 and caused millions of deaths and massive damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28II.29_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News_.28II.29-219">[219]</a></sup> A 2010 United Nations report accused the Rwandan army of committing wide scale human rights violations and crimes against humanity in the Democratic Republic of the Congo during the two Congo wars, charges denied by the Rwandan government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGreal2010_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGreal2010-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rwandan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">Sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rwandan_Civil_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
